With reference to your memoraniim deted 22 April 1964,
requesting & report on tre scatus of the Operational Approval
action on Subject, a memoranium setting forth this informatio:
was forwarded to your office oz 15 Eovezter 1663. It ves re-

turned to CI/CA end wes ezain forvanéed to your office for vor

JFK MICROFILM FILE SUMMARY

SUMMARY; REEL 12, FOLDER(S)_4A & 5 CREATED by
Bryant Rogers
es

SUBJECT OF FOLDER:_LITAMIL-9
201 NUMBER, IF ANY. 329609
INCLUSIVE DATES OF FILE MATERIAL JULY 62 THROUGH AUGUST 72.

RELEVANCE OR NON-RELEVANCE TO OSWALD & JFK ASSASSINAITION:
NONE

REASON OR ASSUMED REASON FOR INCLUSION IN THIS COLLECTION:
In the HSCA testimony of Silvia Duran she indicated |that she
knew him and he was the Cultural Attache at the Cuban
Consulate when she was there. This info was not in the 201
file.

SUMMARY OF INFORMATION WITHIN FILE:

LITAMIL-9 was recruited by the Mexico City Station in late
62 while he was assigned to the Cuban Embassy as Cultural
Attache. He provided the Station intelligence while] he was
in this assignment. He was deactivated in March 1965 when
he returned to Cuba and was seen only occasionally after
that. His contract was terminated in 1970 because of his
lack of access. Only one relevant document was found which
indicated that Proenza, who worked at the Cuban Embassy,
believed that the strong objection to the Mexican Government
by the Cuban Embassy over the Duran's detention was
diplomatic error. This document was processed for release.

CIA/US. GOVERNMENT RELATIONSHIP:
AGENT

PAGES OF NON-JFK-RELATED MATERIAL: 491

Translation of a post card from Kira KOSOVSKA to LITAMIL49.
Kira is the wife of Anguel KOSOVSK", who was a Second Secretary!
in the Bulgarian Embassy in Havana as of October 1965. ghey
are now back in Sofia, Bulgaria. The card was mailed fr

Bulgaria to Cuba.

1

Good morning, Luis! How are you? We are well. We frequently
think of Havana and of our friends (I ~ of a "bored" man too).
After the Black Sea we spent one week in Sofia, and the fol-

lowing week we relaxed at the Radio Sofia tourist
fore leaving for Cuba I worked for Radio Sofia)

house (be~

the Vitusha, near Sofia. The Bulgarians call this mountain

“lungs of the capital". It's a very lovely piace.

eitiee we frannantia faerat cimnta bohelakebhhatated 7

_in the grass and looking at the sky, listening to
Isn't that true? On Vitosha (sic) we remembered all that
We are now in Sofia, preparing to continue our tour through
the mountains. I like to walk a lot, and now I have the —
portunity. We plan to climb the highest peak in Bulgaria |-.
Mus-ala (2925 meters). It isn't difficult ~~ it's not veny

high. What a good country Bulgaria is, but in my
lacks contemplative men. Yes, yes, that's true.
all too practical. Until later, Luis!

Kira KOSOVSKA

Translation of a letter fron Vira KOSOVSYA to LITA TIL-9,
45 the vite of Anguei KUSOVDSEKL, who was a Second Secreta
in the Bulgarian assy in Havana as of Octcher 1965, hey
are now back in Sefia, Buigaria, The letter was nailed
Bulgaria to Cuba,

. i
Good evening, Luis! How have you been? Norking a Jot
as always? Which te choose -- of two opinions on work (‘horses
die from workina" and "work created Nan") it is better tg }
choose the seconc, isn't it?
We are still in Varna, more exactly seme 1S kilometd s!
fron the city of Varna; this doesn't natter because every i
thing here is the area of beaches, hotels, etc. The weather
improved, and new ve go swinmine and sunbathing, but we do !
sO without eagerness -= we are spoiled permanently by thel
Santa Marfa and Atlantic beaches and by the Cuban sunt. At i
the Suu Line de is very Wace Chat nore tnere are no sharks
and one can swim anyxhere one wants,

vay

fe}

In the course cf two years we forgot nany things and
now we are enjoving the Climate, nature, etc, It's true }-
here even the air is absolutely different: ° fresh, healthful,
full of the odors of grass and trees. Some 300 - 499 neters
from the coast the meuntains, covered with forests, begin
Tam very sorry that you, Luis, cannot see al) this, but
an’ an optimist and I am sure that sooner or later you wil t
visit Bulgaria, fc yeu know what they Say about the formation
of the country? When God was dividing the Farth anong th
cnglish, the French, and others, the Bulearian could not dene ‘
because ‘he was working, Then when he came, there was no Jand
left. God scolded but he had to do sonething, Sok
teck a knife and cut a little piece of paradise for the Bul-
garian, an :

Tan not exaggerating -- really the coast of the Blac|
Sea in Bulgaria is very pretty. Now there are about 25:-
thousand foreigners here on vacation, And what is very ine
teresting -- the Majority from the capitalistic ccuntries,
At every step one hears French, German, Swedish. ke have
an acquaintance -- the Manager of one of the hotels; he, fpr

Belgium have heen living in his hotel for 28 days, and that
all are very happy, saving that the vacation in Bulgaria i

. 1. LITAMIL-9 seems to be trapped inefde PZRUMEN. Om 18 August] the

(presumably by an airline crew member), used the term "de lo mas bien," This
is an indicator meaning "I expect w leave within s year." In another (undated)
letter L-9 reports that he has been promoted to “Secretario de Segunda?

is dofag @ lot of vaintine since he hac mor var Some eel wm erele OL eee d oe

of material requested indicates that he expects to remain inside for gpme time.

that he had spoken with L-9. L*9 said he did aot expect to leave for i"a long

time." '

Europe it may be difficult for L<9 to obtain a foreien post. Tt is not likely
that he could seriously be considered politically reliable by the PBRUMEN
Government, With the return of his cother and sister from Spaix he no |longer
has an excuse to request permission to visit Madrid. The only bright igpot
om the horizon is his sister-in=law’s close relationship to AMTHUG. L317 feels

Translation of 2 post card fron Kira KOSOVSEA.to LITAMEL-9,
Kira is the wife of Anzuel KOSOVSKI, whe was a Second ecretary
in the Bulgarian I assy in Havana as of Cctcher 1963, They
are now back in Sofia, Bulgaria, The card was nailed trom
Bulgaria to Cuba,

Dear Luis, how are you? Before leaving ! called veu tq verify
your address and, of course, to say "the lest goodbye" (for
three nontks!), hut yeu weren't there. Surely vou had your
mind on the countryside after the hurricane, If yeu cid,
I wish that you cculd climb like during the fifteen days of
Girén, that would suit you very well,

I cars)

te have been in Buloaria for three dave now: ane daw ¥
and two in Varna in the guest house of the Bulgarian ‘{INREX, f
‘ . The trip wert fine, but it was very faticuing; we couldn't
sleep because it wasn't night -- at 9 the sun set and at 12
cane out again. In Prague ve spent one cay while waiting

for the plane to S-fia, We are living like Counts ef Luxem-
bourg in a luxury hotel. Ir Sofia everything is fine. | It

is quite hot during the day, but the nights are very colld.

Here in Varna it's the same story, but ali the hotels are

full of tourists who get brave and go sw ng in the ners

sea. As for us, we haven't gone swimming t. And generally
after Cuba I am indifferent to the sea, Luis, until later.

Kira KOSCVSKA

Translation of a post card from Kira KOSOVSKA to LITAMIL-§.

ira i- the wife of Anguel KOSOVSEI, who was a Second Sec etary
in the Bulgarian Embassy in Havana as of October 1965. ey
are now back in Sofia, Bulgaria. The card was mailed fro
Bulgaria to Cuba.

Good morning, Luis! How are you? We are well. We frequently
think of Havana and of our friends (I - of 2 "bored" man 00).
After the Black Sea we spent one weex in Sofia, and the fol-

lowing week we relaxed at the Radio Sofia tourist house (be-

fore leaving for Cuba I worked for Radio Sofia), located on

the Vitusha, near Sofia. The Bulgarians call this mountain

“lungs of the capital". It's a very lovely place. Living in
Ceti, wo Sac gee ely Dea gel olaple pleasuses == dyiug woe

in the grass and looking at the sky, listening to the silence.
Isn't that true? On Vitosha (sic) we remembered all that
We are now in Sofia, preparing to continue our tour through
the mountains. I like to walk a iot, and now I have the —
portunity. We plan to climb the highest peak in Bulgaria |--
Mus-ala (2925 meters). {It isn't difficult -~ it's not very
bigh. What a good country Bulgaria is, but in zy opinion |she
lacks contemplative men. Yes, yes, that's true. They are
all too practical. Until later, Luis!

- Kira KOSOVSKA

1, LITAHIL-9 seems to be trapped inside PBL’ MEN. On 18 Acgugt the
Case Officer met with LITAMIL-17 (L-9's brother) to review two letters received
from 1-9, One of these, dated 15 July and mpiled at Gander, Kewfoundland
(presumably by aa airline crew member), used the term "de lo mas died." This
is an indicator -ceaning "I expect t leave within @ year.” In another (undated)
letter L-9 reports that he has been promoted co “Secretario de Segunda!

2. Le9 asked for @ large quantity of art supplies and mentioned that he
fe Selig 6 lek Cl peluclug elmce ine nee nue yee yvec vera co wurn, dne qusaticy

of material requested indicates that he expects to remain inside for|some time.

3. The C/O asked L-17 to phone L=9, ostensibly to request further detsil
on how to ship the art supplies, Io the course of the conversation t-17 was to
ask L~3 how long ke expected to remain im PBRUMEM. L-l7 reported om |28 August
that he had spoken with L-9, L-9 said he did not expect to leave for “a long
tine.”

ae OF content

1. On 18 February 1963 Sori Coulibaly, the Ambassador of the
Republic of Mali to the United Nations and to Cuba,ll| and
Mamadou Traore, Deputy Permanent Representative of t| e Mali
Mission to the United Nations, arrived in Mexico fro Habana,

Mexico City that he had spoken with Raul Roa, Cuban Foreign
Minister, who asked Coulibaly to take steps to have the
Government of Mali send a resident Ambassador to Cuba. :

2. Coulibaly said that the Cubans had put Pressure on him to
open an office in Habana and that they had in fact given hin
a building for this Purpose. However, Coulibaly said that
he did not see how Mali could afford to open an offi¢e in
Habanz, in view of the fact that he had hardly enoug money
to operate the Mali Mission to the United Nations.2

3. Coulibaly and Traore left Mexico City on 20 February |for
New York. Coulibaly carried Mali diplomatic passport No. 23;
Traore carried diplomatic passport No. 42.

1. Headquarters Comment. Coulibaly presented his credentials
a Cuba on ebruary 1963.

budget for the operation of the Mali Mission tot
United Nations; that he had been allotted only on
of that amount for the first Quarter of 1963; and| that
he had not received even that. .

SUBJECT: LITAMIL-9 and the Latin American Writerts Congress
_ in Mexico

1, The undersigned reviewed the list of delegates

, attending the Latin American Writer's Congress with L-9

- on 19 March 1967. The latter indicated he knew all the

* members af the Cohan dalanatian = Alain CADBCNTICD Catanne

- Roberto FERNANDEZ Retamar, Lizandro OTERO, Nicolas GUILLEN
and Pablo neREDA, a Chilean writer whom he first met some
25 years ago and saw again about 1962. L-9 stressed he
. did not know the Cuban delegates to the point of calling
- anyone of them a personal friend as his dealings with then
~ had been confined to professional contacts when he worked
- for the Nationai cultural Councit. He had never been in-
- vited to their homes or invited them to his. The delegate
~ he felt most at ease with was Alejo CARPENTIER with whom he
"= felt he had more in common than with the others. CARPENTIER
_~ who has a French father and white Russian mother lived many
~ years in France and spent some time in South America. L-9

~ considered him to be an. intellectual of definite "bourgeois"

for his novels (L-9 recalled that his name had once been
mentioned in connection with the Nobel Prize for literature)
~ and his journalistic writing (L-9 still remeabered some lof
the articles regularly written by him in Paris for the
~ “El Mundo" daily in the pre Castro eral) but he is also
an established music critic and a connaisseur of modern
painting, all in all a talented and most impressive man
_ fiw in his sixties, ,

; 2. L-9 had on many occasions offered to helP WOFACT
~ in any way possible. The undersigned pointed out that he
now had a unique opportunity to do this with the Writer's
Congress. WOF ACT was interested in assessing the Cuban
- representatives at this Congress to determine their
- possible vulnerability to recruitment. It was also ine
terested in hearing from the Cuban delegates what they

— thought of the Congress and it's accomplishments since it
~ Was apparent that the great majority of it's members were
— Communist sympathizers and would probably use the Congress
~- for political Purposes. Any information on the situation
— in Cuba and on Cuban Government organizations, particularly
“on the incorporation of the National Cultural Council into
~ the Ministry of Education would be appreciated. ft would
~ also be interesting to know why Cintio VITIER who was

~ scheduled to come to the Congress did not show up. L-9.
sald he was willing to help but. was extremely busy with

his brother's edible of! business In Toluca. it would be

2 |

~ sifficuit for him to find tine w talk with the Cuban
delegates, he felt .in addition,that it wuld be difficult
for him to simply walk In on the delegates if he could] not
be invited, officially, to the Congress or to a social
. affair connected with it. Finally, L-9 pointed out tht
~ he had now been in Mexico for nearly six months, that
— “everyone” knew that he had no Intention of returning to

— Cuba and that, for these reasons, the Cuban delegates to

the SConcrcre mtaht nat Be sete 4 eee el ee eeel

~ it was decided that L-9 would call the next morning on
; ~ Ambassador Joaquin HERNANDEZ Armas who had just returned
a from Cuba. L-9 would pay his respects and find out if|the
~- Embassy planned some secial function at which he could
~- openly meet the Cuban delegates (he felt he might wrangle
~ an invitation to such an affair either directly from the
~ Ambassador or from Heberto JCRRIN, the ex-Embassy portero
- whom he has known for years). It was further decided that
~ &-9 would concentrate on CARPENTIER with whom he felt He
~ had the best rapport and who was in his view the delegate
_ with the most "bourgeois" background.
~ 3. At a-meeting held on 21 March L-9 related that| he
~ had seen Ambassador HERNANDEZ earlier that morning (the
- delegates to the Writer's Congress which had been held for
the last few days In Guadalajara were scheduled to return

the next day}. He had found the Ambassador nervous and. pre-

occupied, The latter told him almost mechanically they , i
3

everything in Cuba (political and economic situat fon, sugar
harvest, etc) was fine. He informed L-9 that he did not

have the Opportunity to see L-9'%s5 Sister-in-law and that

-be had given a letter, which L-9 had asked him to deliver |to

her for passage to the National Cultural Council to Martal

GONZALEZ of the International Relations Bureau of the

- Council. L-9, in this letter, asked that his three month
leave from the Cultural Council be greatly extended. The
Ambassador said he ignored what reaction the Cultural
Peopte had to his letter. He explained that the Cultural

Congress. He said that he did not think that a party
would be held at the Embassy for the delegates and did not
~ offer to put L-9 in contact with the people he wanted to
. see. Since he did not seem to have gotten anywhere with the

JORR IN confirmed that the Embassy would not have a party
for the Congress delegates “because of the Semana Santa,"
and said he did not know exactly when the delegates would
drop in the Embassy following their return from Guadalajara.
Upon leaving JORRIN ,t-9 went to the Del Prado where he was
told that the Congress delegates would only return to Mekico
late that day. A few blocks from the hotel L-9 ran into
Nicolas GUILLEN who greeted him by. saying “here is L-9 in
his ambiente Mexicano." The two men walked together back
to the Del Prado. GUILLEN turned down L-9's invitation for
@ cup of coffee saying he had to visit someone. He did
ment ton that the Congress, as far as he was concerned, was
“una basura" and told L- 9 that he had flown from Guadalajara
an oy

‘— fiem position against the “Imperialists." After relating

- to Mexico City (he did not say why) ahead of the other
- Cuban delegates wno were seturning by ruad tater that day.
— GUILLEN told L-9 that he would be in the same neighborhood
early next day and would be glad to have coffee with him |if
L+9 could meet him then. Anyway, he added, he would be
staying in Mexico for another two weeks at the request of
the Ambassador. They could see each other again later on
before he left. As they were about to cross a busy street
shortly before parting, L-9 took GUILLEN dy the arm in a

— friendiy yesuuse. The lottos pulied may and '-a had the

~ feeling that GUILLEN did not want to let L-9 be friendly
— with him, .
- S. The next meeting with L-9 was held on 24 March.
- L-a said that he had not been able to call on the Cubans
- at the Gel Prado until! earlier that day. He had run inta
- Licandro OTERO while in the:lobby. The latter told him he
_. Was about to leave. When L-9 said "already?" OTERO pointed
- out that he had been in Mexico for two weeks already.
- L°9 repeated the derogatory. remarks made about the Congress
~ by GUILLEN. OTERO said that, on the contrary, this had
~ been a successful meeting, A letter of protest had been

~ $ent to President Johnson and the Congress had taken a

- the above, L-9 recalled that a rumor circulated in Havana,

- shortly before his departure from Cuba, to the effect. that

- Marcia LEISECA, OTERO'S wife {a woman of about 34 who
- worked at the Casa de las Americas) was about to divorce
- OTERO to marry Osmani ClENFUEGOS. L-9 added that Marcja
- had relatives in Mexico whom she visited in 1962 and 1965.
~ After leaving OTERO, L-9 phoned CARPENTER and was told
by the latter to meet him the next day,
- 6 L+9 and CARPENTIER met for breekfast on 2h March,
- When L-9 asked him for news about the National Cultural
- Council, CARPENTIER said that L~9 knew certainly more about
~ that then he did as he had been in France since last November.
~ CARPENTIER claimed that he had been called in by OORTICOS
last October and told a CASTILLANOS, the cutrent
-- Cuban Ambassador in Paris/had requested his nNomination| to
the Paris Embassy as Minister Concellor. CARPENTIER said
he tried to get out of this two year assignment which he
found too long, but was told by DORTICOS that there was |no
way out of it. The Cuban Government, said DORTICOS, was
— Out to make it's representation in Paris “an absolutely
- first class Embassy", DoRTICos added that CARPENTIER would
not be so busy in Paris that he wald not find time to wriite.
Whether he found time to write CARPENTIER did not say.
— What he did say was that the Ambassador: who was doing a
very good job,did an enormous amount of work and usually
worked late at night. He also mentioned that while in

Paris or shortly before arriving there he had gone to Hanoi

on an official mission, CARPERT IER gave no details
ether then tc say that that horrible war was probably
going to last, and that U.S. planes had flown right over

information but gathered that CARPENTIER remained in
North Vietnam two or three weeks. ‘
7. &-9 asked why VITIER had not attended the Congress.
CARPENTIER replied that VITIER was “in a special situation
in Cuba" as he was not in accord with the revolution,
He had been given the opportunity to go to Spain for |the
Cuban Government but had refused to go. VITIER undoubtedly
knew, from the background of the delegates, that the Writer's
Congress in Mexico would be a leftist affair. CARPENTIER
guessed that he probably declined to come because of this.
Talking about himself, CARPENTIER said (without further
details) that he would be going to Moscow in May. Hel
announced that a film based on his novel "Los Pasos Perdidos"
would be made this year, probably haif in France and haif
in Cuba (negotiations with the French are still going] on).
Finally, he mentioned that he was trying to convince the
Cuban Government to create a centralized publishing depare
ment and that as Director of the Cuban National printing
office, before leaving Cuba, he had succeeded in gett}ng

some 70 million books printed. He mentioned, incidentally,

8

that his publisher in Mexico.is Arnaldo SAFILA, ex director

of the Mexico City Fondo del Cultura Economica whom

CARPENTIER said he was on his way to see to collect rayalties.

CARPENTIER said he would leave Mexico on 29 March via |SABENA

and agreed to get together with L-9 on 27 March,
